============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG7)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P**c9
Candidate formulas: 73

GT depends **only on P** (t does not appear) and has the form
\[
0.721355\Big[(-1+P/6.6511035)(1-P/13.5380926)P + (1-P/13.5380926)P + P^{1/3}\Big].
\]
Expand the polynomial part:
- First term: \((-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P = -P + P^2(1/a+1/b) - P^3/(ab)\).
- Second term: \((1-P/b)P = P - P^2/b\).
Adding them cancels the \(\pm P\), leaving
\[
\text{GT} = 0.721355\Big[ P^2\Big(\frac1a+\frac1b-\frac1b\Big) - \frac{P^3}{ab} + P^{1/3}\Big]
= 0.721355\Big[\frac{1}{a}P^2 - \frac{1}{ab}P^3 + P^{1/3}\Big].
\]
So GT is exactly a linear combination of \(P^{1/3}, P^2, P^3\) with **no constant term and no \(P^1\) term**:
\[
\text{GT} = A\,P^{1/3} + B\,P^2 + C\,P^3
\]
where \(A=0.721355\), \(B=0.721355/a\), \(C=-0.721355/(ab)\), with \(a=6.6511035\), \(b=13.5380926\).

Therefore any candidate can match iff it can be reduced (by setting its free constants) to exactly \(c_0 P^{1/3} + c_2 P^2 + c_1 P^3\) and eliminate any other dependence (constants, \(t\), sin/log/exp, rational terms, Max/Abs, extra powers).

Now check candidates:

1. Has constant term and a complicated sin(log(exp(P*c8+c9*t)+1)) term. To match GT for all \(t\), must kill the sin term by setting its coefficient \(c4=0\). Then still has constant \(c3\) which must be 0. Remaining is \(c0 P^{1/3}+c2 P^2+c1 P^3\), which can match by choosing \(c0=A, c2=B, c1=C\). **Matches**.

2. Has \(P*c3\), \(P*c4*sin(c5*t+c6)\), and constant \(c7\). Must set \(c4=0\) (remove \(t\)), \(c3=0\) (no linear term), \(c7=0\) (no constant). Left with \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

3. Has \(P^2*c3*sin(c4+c5*t)\) plus extra \(P^2*c6\) and constant \(c7\). Set \(c3=0\) to remove \(t\), set \(c7=0\). Combine \(P^2\) coefficients: \(c2+c6\) can be set to \(B\). **Matches**.

4. Has extra \(P^{1/3}*c1*sin(c2*t+c3)\), plus constant \(c6\). Set \(c1=0\) to remove \(t\), set \(c6=0\). Remaining \(c0 P^{1/3}+c5 P^2+c4 P^3\). **Matches**.

5. Has constant \(c3\) and \(c4*sin(c5+c6*t)\). Set \(c4=0\), \(c3=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

6. Has rational terms with \(t\): \(P*c3/(c4*t+c5)\) and \(c7/(c4*t+c5)\) plus constant \(c6\). To remove \(t\)-dependence for all \(t\), must set \(c3=0\) and \(c7=0\). Then set \(c6=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

7. Has \(P*c3*Max(0,P*c4+c5)\) and constant \(c6\). To avoid non-polynomial piecewise term, set \(c3=0\). Then set \(c6=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

8. Has \(P^{c3} c4 exp(P c5)\) and constant \(c6\). Must remove exponential term: set \(c4=0\). Then set \(c6=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

10. Has \(c3*exp(P*c4)\) plus constant \(c5\). Set \(c3=0\), \(c5=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

14. Has constant \(c3\) and log term. Set \(c4=0\), \(c3=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

15. Has \(P*c3\), plus \(P*c4*(c5*Abs(P))^{c6}\), plus constant \(c7\). Set \(c4=0\) to remove Abs/power term; set \(c3=0\); set \(c7=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

16. Entire expression is something/(P+c1). GT is not a rational function with a pole; to match for all P would require numerator to be divisible by (P+c1) and reduce to polynomial+fractional power \(P^{1/3}\) (but numerator contains \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P^{4/3}\) terms, division by (P+c1) will not yield pure \(P^{1/3}\) term for all P unless those coefficients are zero). If set those fractional-power numerator coefficients to 0, you lose \(P^{1/3}\) entirely. No way to produce standalone \(P^{1/3}\) without denominator. **No match**.

17. Has \(P^{c4}c5 exp(P c6)\) plus constant \(c7\) and linear term \(P*c3\). Set \(c5=0\) to remove exp term; set \(c3=0\); set \(c7=0\). Remaining \(P^2,P^3\) only (no \(P^{1/3}\)). But could set one of \(P^2\) coefficients to represent \(P^{1/3}\)? No, powers fixed. So cannot. **No match**.

18. Has \(P^{1/5} c0 exp(P c1)\) (not removable to \(P^{1/3}\) unless kill it), plus \(P*c4\), plus \(P^{c5}c6\), constant. If kill exp term by \(c0=0\), then need \(P^{1/3}\) from \(P^{c5}c6\) (set \(c5=1/3,c6=A\)), set \(c4=0\), constant \(c7=0\), and set \(P^2,P^3\) coefficients accordingly. **Matches**.

19. Similar to 18 but has extra \(P*c5\). Set \(c0=0\) (remove exp term), set \(c4=0\) and \(c5=0\) (remove linear terms), set \(c8=0\), and use \(P^{c6}c7\) for \(P^{1/3}\). **Matches**.

20. Has \(P*c3\), plus \(P*c4*log(c5*Abs(P)+1)\), plus constant \(c6\). Set \(c4=0\), \(c3=0\), \(c6=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

21. Has \(P*c?\) no, has \(P*c3\) and \(P^{c3}c4\)?? Actually term is \(P**c3*c4\) plus constant \(c5\). Also has \(P*c? \) none besides that. Set constant \(c5=0\). Use \(P^{c3}c4\) to supply either \(P^2\) or \(P^3\) or \(P^{1/3}\), but only one such flexible power term; the other two powers are fixed \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P^2,P^3\) already present. Since candidate already has \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), \(P^3\) fixed, we can just set \(c3\) (the exponent) term coefficient \(c4=0\) to remove it. Then it matches. **Matches**.

22. Has \(P^2\), \(P\), and two flexible power terms plus constant. Set \(c6=0\), set linear term \(c1=0\). Use \(P^{c2}c3\) for \(P^{1/3}\) (set \(c2=1/3,c3=A\)) and \(P^{c4}c5\) for \(P^3\) (set \(c4=3,c5=C\)), and set \(c0=B\). **Matches**.

23. Has piecewise Max and Abs terms; can eliminate by setting coefficients \(c3=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then constant \(c7=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

24. Has log(exp(P^{1/3}*... + P^2*...)+1) plus constant. Must set \(c4=0\) to remove log term; then set \(c3=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

25. Has \(P*c3*log(P*c4+1)\) plus constant \(c5\). Set \(c3=0\), \(c5=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

26. Like 16 but fewer terms; still overall /(P+c1) and cannot yield pure polynomial + \(P^{1/3}\) without denominator. Same obstruction. **No match**.

27. Has Max terms; can set their coefficients \(c0=0\) and \(c2=0\) to remove them. Then use \(P^{c4}c5\) for \(P^{1/3}\) and constant \(c6=0\). But then no \(P^2\) or \(P^3\) terms remain. So cannot. **No match**.

28. Has Max terms and linear term \(P*c7\). Could set Max coefficients \(c0=0\), \(c5=0\), set \(c7=0\), constant \(c8=0\). Remaining \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4} = c2*c3^{c4} * P^{c4+1}\), only one power term, cannot produce simultaneously \(P^2\) and \(P^3\) and \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

29. Has rational terms in P: \(P*c3/(P*c4+c5)\) and \(c7/(P*c4+c5)\) plus constant \(c6\). To match polynomial, set \(c3=0\), \(c7=0\), \(c6=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

30. Has constant \(c4\) and nonlinear \((c6*exp(P*c7)+1)^{c8}\). Set \(c5=0\) to remove that whole term; set \(c4=0\). Then it has \(P*c3\) which must be 0. Remaining \(P^2,P^3\) only (no \(P^{1/3}\)). **No match**.

31. Has log term and constant. Set \(c3=0\) to remove log term; set \(c5=0\). Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches**.

32. Has Max terms producing higher-order piecewise polynomials and no explicit \(P^3\) term; also no way to get \(P^{1/3}\) except the first term yes. But the Max terms are \(P^2*Max(0,P+c2)\) and \(P*Max(0,P+c4)\) which are piecewise \(P^3\) etc; to be globally polynomial for all real P would require zeroing them: set their coefficients \(c1=0\), \(c3=0\). Then only \(P^{1/3}\) plus constant \(c5\) remains; cannot get \(P^2,P^3\). **No match**.

33. Pure polynomial terms \(P^3\), multiple \(P^2\), \(P\), plus a flexible power term and constant. Set linear terms \(c4=0,c5=0\), constant \(c8=0\). Use \(P^{c6}c7\) for \(P^{1/3}\) (set \(c6=1/3,c7=A\)). Combine \(P^2\) coefficients to \(B\), set \(P^3\) coefficient to \(C\). **Matches**.

34. Has \(P^2\), \(P\), \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}=const*P^{c4+1}\), plus \(P^{c6}c7\), plus constant. Can set \(c1=0\), \(c5=0\), \(c8=0\). Use \(P^{c6}c7\) for \(P^{1/3}\). Use \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}\) for \(P^3\) by setting \(c4=2\) (then power 3) and scaling. Then \(P^2*c0\) gives \(P^2\). **Matches**.

35. Has \(P^3,P^2,P\), plus \(P^{c4}c5\), plus constant. Set \(c3=0\), \(c6=0\). Use \(P^{c4}c5\) for \(P^{1/3}\). Set \(P^2\) and \(P^3\) coefficients. **Matches**.

36. Has extra nonlinear \((P*c6+1)^3\) term and constant. To match, must set \(c5=0\) (remove cubic-in-P expansion) and set constant \(c4=0\). Then it has \(P\) term \(c1\) which must be 0. Remaining \(P^2\) and \(P^{c2}c3\). Can set \(c2=1/3,c3=A\), but no \(P^3\) term. **No match**.

44. Has \(P^3\), \(P^2\) terms, and \(P*c3*(P*c4)^{c5}=const*P^{c5+1}\). No \(P^{1/3}\) source. **No match**.
